< Text>
I've been to many AFs' and this one is hands down the most cleanly and where I feel the safest. If you have any problems with fellow members or the environment the manager, Michele, takes every step to make sure you feel at home and takes care of the problem. The best thing is that it's a tight run ship which means I don't have to worry about equipment laying around everywhere, if I need something it is always in its place,  the bathrooms are sanitary so I feel comfortable changing there after work and people aren't hogging up machines or weights because they are on their phones. I feel safe knowing that you must use your key fob to get in and the guest door remains locked, the cubbies where everyone puts their belongings is close to the guest door and yes the area is safe but things still happen so I like this extra precaution. When someone comes to the door Michele walks up right away and lets them in during office hours, I really like the screening process, I'm not cool with random people just walking in and working out. I think it's comical that she has signs everywhere reminding people of the rules because there are a lot of them but it's crazy how members still do not follow any of them so the more signs the merrier. The membership is inexpensive and I've never had any problems with billing or fees, that's rare when any company uses a third party for taking the automatic monthly payments. I think this club's motto is respect, if you respect the staff and club rules you'll always be welcome.</Text>

< date>

<Rate>1< /Rate>< Review>
Unfortunately after changing managers I had to change a once excellent review. Thai Time Bistro in Ocean Beach does not have consistency among chefs. Before the old chef took over as manager you could order any dish without fish sauce. Now you can only get those dishes without fish sauce when she is there. So vegan options are very limited. They also don't tell you there is fish sauce in things when you order a vegetarian option. You must inquire each visit, and ask if you can get it without the fish sauce. The manager told me any of the chefs can prepare the dish without fish sauce. But I have been told repeatedly by other wait staff that getting items without fish sauce is not an option for the chef that is cooking. I have spoken to them multiple times telling them cohesion is really important. But they basically told me that they are not catering to vegetarians or vegans. So I figured a shout out was important. I won't be eating there anymore. Unfortunately there isn't another Thai place in walking distance :(< /Review>

< review>
This place is good, we sometimes stop by for lunch. Our usual orders are the Panang curry , the pad thai, and the beef noodles. For lunch they have combos with an entree, a soup & salad, and an egg roll for $12 or up to $16 depending on the meat you order with it.

Update 4/20/18

Owners have changed, food took too long to bring out (some of our party got their food 45 min after us) and the recipes are different as well. Got my usual Pad Thai and there was just no flavor. Can't recommend anymore.</review>

The good: I used GrubHub  to order, and my order arrived 15 minutes before expected. Food was a perfect temperature to dive right in.
The okay: The crab angel appetizers were just slightly overcooked,  a bit too brown at the edges. And with a subtle but odd salty taste.
The not so good: I noted on order that I wanted MILD, not spicy. My panang curry is definitely spicy, probably moderately spiced for some, but too spicy for me.  I also asked that the driver call when he arrived, so I was startled when there was a knock and no call.
I have eaten at all the Thai Time restaurants in San Diego,  always enjoy the food. But they went just a little off mark with this online order.</Text>

<rating>1</rating><name>Ryan Cox< /name>< Review>
DO NOT EVEN THINK ABOUT RENTING AN APARTMENT HERE!!!!!  I had an extremely negative experience from beginning to end.  First of all, Elaine is extremely condescending, rude, and takes advantage of first time and young renters.  Upon move-in, it was clear that the apartment had serious mold and trapped moisture issues.  Elaine rushed through our move-in inspection, probably hoping that we would overlook some issues.  The carpet was soaking wet because they had kept the windows closed after it had been cleaned.  When we brought the issue to the attention of management, Elaine gave us a box of carpet fresh with only about 1/4 of the container left to "get rid of the smell."  I was far more concerned about getting sick from the obvious mold.  When we moved in, Elaine also made a point to say that the apartment had been "professionally" painted, but it was obvious that this was not the case as there were paint drips all over the floor in the bathroom and kitchen.  In the winter, mold developed around the window in the bedroom and the sliding glass door in the living room.  When we asked maintenance about it, they said it was just something we had to keep under control with bleach.  Maybe if they had installed double-paned windows or updated the aging apartments in any way, it wouldn't be so much of an issue.  The carpets were always damp in the winter, and nothing ever dried out in this apartment, especially towels in the bathroom or dishes in the kitchen.  Depending on where your apartment is located, you will either be boiling hot and in direct sun or (in our case) never see the true light of day.  The kitchen and bathroom were always dark, no matter what time of day it was.  The shower never kept the same temperature for more than 30 seconds at a time, and the toilet clogged extremely easily.  We consistently had to unclog our toilet once or twice a day.  If you try to adhere anything to the wall, huge paint chunks will come off when removing these items because they slap a new coat of paint on every time someone moves out.  They increased the price of laundry in the middle of the pandemic when people were doing their worst financially.  They recently were taken over by a new leasing company and seem to have replaced the entire leasing office staff - thank god.  The bar set by the previous management was so low that I was pleased to learn the new staff was actually conscientious and pleasant when I interacted with them.  But at least the old management picked up the phone when I called the office!  It has been such a nightmare trying to move out of this place.  I had to schedule a move-out inspection for three separate dates because they "lost" the paperwork for the first two.  When it came time for the third attempt at an inspection, I called to make sure they hadn't forgotten, and they had once again!  I was able to schedule one for two days after this third date, which happened to be a Sunday.  It was scheduled for 10AM and I was told to arrive at the office at 9:45.  They neglected to understand their own operating hours because they don't open until 11AM on Sundays.  At this point I had already moved into a new place, so they wasted an hour of my Sunday morning.  When I came back to the office at 11AM, I was told that they didn't have any maintenance staff onsite and that they don't do inspections on Sundays.
Then why did they schedule my inspection for a Sunday in the first place?!  Since my lease was up the next day, I turned in my keys and was told that an inspection would happen that week.  It's been nearly two months since my lease ended and they still haven't returned my security deposit.  I'm not even sure that an inspection ever happened, as I haven't received an itemized list of repairs either.  I even gave them my forwarding address.  I call them about once a week to check in, and they almost never return my calls.  I've been more than lenient and beyond flexible with their both legal obligation and treatment of me and am having to take legal action just to get what is owed to me.<//Review>

<Rating>3</Rating>< Text>
I lived at Cypress Point for six years, moving out last month. Over that time there were a series of managers and management companies. It seemed expensive, but comparable in price and amenities to other two-bedroom  rentals in Santa Cruz that allowed pets.

Past issues, especially in the first year or so, included old, worn appliances and cabinets with covered with layers of paint; blinds and vinyl flooring that was so evenly dingy that I hadn't realized they weren't supposed to be that color; laundry rooms that always had at least one "broken" washer; announced and unannounced water shutoffs sometimes on a weekly basis; water leakage from the upstairs plumbing into my walls; and the danged notes (sometimes water shutoff warnings) taped to my front door which tore the paint off in strips. Naturally, the rent increased by 3% every year.

The positives:
The laundry and plumbing problems have been fixed. The cost per load has increased a bit, but the machines work well. Note: there are three laundry rooms for this large apartment complex, so be prepared to schlep things a ways and compete with others for time at the machines.
The gym has been upgraded and now has more equipment (but no restroom).
The pool area is nicer than it was.
Some of the apartments are currently being renovated and I've seen cabinetry and wall-to-wall carpets going into dumpsters (yay!)... I hope they're doing my old place now.
When I left, landscaping over/under-watering issues were being gradually addressed, so the grounds look much nicer, but you might watch out for one or two lawn areas that are chronically overwatered and so are slippery.
The maintenance crew is responsive about repair requests. And they're nice guys.
The dumpster areas are kept cleaner, discouraging the raccoons and crows.
The current employees are professional and friendly. I enjoyed my chats with Elaine, who was usually the one who helped me out with laundry card refills.
Florina, the manager, was always friendly with me.

There was always a cookie jar in the office for my dogs, and they knew it.

The 3 stars are for the overall, six-year experience.< /Text>

< text>
I was sent to Reche Canyon from Kaiser, Fontana  after 15 days in the Hospital, flat on my back. I am 85 years old and midway through my stay at Kaiser I had surgery to repair a torn diaphragm and liver from a broken rib. When they discharged me to Reche Canyon I had not been out of bed for 15 days. I arrived at Reche Canyon on Easter Sunday, April 16th with Oxygen @ 2% and couldn't even sit up by myself. The staff was wonderful, attentive, the food wan't too bad and best of all - NO SMELL. They worked with me every day and I was discharged on April 29th without any oxygen and able to get up out of bed and walking around the facility on my own, with a walker of course. I am very happy with the care I was given  here and would recommend this facility to anyone who must go to a skilled nursing facility.</text>

< Text>
I hate to even give this place one star but I have to because it won't let me choose zero stars. BEWARE!  Worst place ever!!  My 22 year old son was sent here from Kaiser with a brain injury.  We only had four options of sub acute care facilities to choose from and Reche Canyon was the best of the worst. The first time he was sent there he was only there for four days when he had to be rushed back to the hospital with pneumonia as well as an unstageable bed wound (did not have this when he was discharged from Kaiser 4 days prior).  The bed wound was later staged at a stage 4. He was sent back to Reche Canyon two weeks later where his bed wound continued to get worse (down to his bone). Within a two month timeframe he was in the emergency room at Loma Linda 3 different times. The last straw for me was when they ended up having to bag him (CPR) because his oxygen saturation dropped below 50%, he was sent to the emergency room at Loma Linda where he then was transferred to Kaiser with pneumonia for the third time, a completely out of control bed wound,  and a staph infection. After that I did everything I could not to let them send him back to Reche Canyon. Reche Canyon almost killed my son due to the lack of care. I was there every single day with my son but they do not allow anybody to stay past 9 PM. So between 9:00 PM and the next day only God knows what they did with my son or didn't do with my son.  Plenty of times staff there would tell me that they are understaffed and this is why some patients don't get tended to properly, especially the patients that don't have family members to speak up for them. If your family member cannot speak for themselves DO NOT send them here. I have educated myself on patients rights and learned how to be an excellent advocate for my son.</Text>

< name>
Teddy S.<//name>
<review>Tin Lizzie is a great spot! All the bartenders are very friendly and the regulars make you feel at home. The drinks are strong and they have a decent selection of beers, including Stella and Kona IPA. There's no food. Occasionally, snack bowls can be found with chips and nuts.
The entrance from the parking lot leads directly to a small and dark space with no windows. You'll immediately find a pool table and an old-school cigarette machine with the pull handles. The bar counter lines one wall and opposite that are refurbished banquettes with cocktail tables.
Tufted leather abounds and covers the banquettes, underneath the bar counter and the bathroom doors. Everything else is exposed brick. It adds a nice ambiance. The bathrooms are done up in subway tile. One each for guys and gals - single occupancy only. They're surprisingly and refreshingly clean.
A couple of flat screens are always turned to a movie or a football game and there's a touchtunes jukebox playing anything from Shania to The Roots. Be careful though, everyone pays extra to skip ahead!< /review></record>
</dataset><record>

Went on Friday night, usually best quality is offered at buffets on this day; Saturday and Sunday as well.

Everything looked like it was from the Lunch buffet and was dry or overly oily, the fresh BBQ was serving rancid meat--you know that taste when beef is semi-ok but has the spoiled taste and smell to it.

I will never be back here.

New Panda Buffet a mile or so West is much better and cheaper, this place just looks nice.</review>
